      <p>South Africa also has one possession, the small <a href="/wiki/Subantarctic" title="Subantarctic">sub-Antarctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of the Prince Edward Islands, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Marion_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Marion Island">Marion Island</a> (290&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> or 110&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and Prince Edward Island (45&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> or 17&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) (not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Canadian province of the same name</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_South_Africa" title="Climate of South Africa">Climate of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg/280px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg/420px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg/560px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1458" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_ZAF_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of South Africa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa has a generally <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a> because it is surrounded by the Atlantic and Indian Oceans on three sides, because it is located in the climatically milder <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, and because its average elevation rises steadily toward the north (toward the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>) and further inland. This varied topography and oceanic influence result in a great variety of climatic zones. The climatic zones range from the extreme desert of the southern <a href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Namib Desert">Namib</a> in the farthest northwest to the lush subtropical climate in the east along the border with Mozambique and the Indian Ocean. Winters in South Africa occur between June and August. </p>
      <p>The extreme southwest has a climate remarkably similar to that of the Mediterranean Sea with wet winters and hot, dry summers, hosting the famous <a href="/wiki/Fynbos" title="Fynbos">fynbos</a> <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biome</a> of <a href="/wiki/Shrubland" title="Shrubland">shrubland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albany_thickets" title="Albany thickets">thicket</a>. This area also produces much of the wine in South Africa. This region is also particularly known for its wind, which blows intermittently almost all year. The severity of this wind made passing around the Cape of Good Hope particularly treacherous for sailors, causing many shipwrecks. Further east on the south coast, rainfall is distributed more evenly throughout the year, producing a green landscape. This area is popularly known as the <a href="/wiki/Garden_Route" title="Garden Route">Garden Route</a>. </p>
      <p>The Free State is particularly flat because it lies centrally on the high plateau. North of the <a href="/wiki/Vaal_River" title="Vaal River">Vaal River</a>, the Highveld becomes better watered and does not experience subtropical extremes of heat. Johannesburg, in the centre of the Highveld, is at 1,740&nbsp;m (5,709&nbsp;ft) above sea level and receives an annual rainfall of 760&nbsp;mm (29.9&nbsp;in). Winters in this region are cold, although snow is rare. </p>
      <p>The high <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a> mountains, which form the south-eastern escarpment of the Highveld, offer limited skiing opportunities in winter. The coldest place on mainland South Africa is Buffelsfontein in the Eastern Cape, where a temperature of −20.1&nbsp;°C (−4.2&nbsp;°F) was recorded in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The Prince Edward Islands have colder average annual temperatures, but Buffelsfontein has colder extremes. The deep interior of mainland South Africa has the hottest temperatures: a temperature of 51.7&nbsp;°C (125.06&nbsp;°F) was recorded in 1948 in the Northern Cape Kalahari near <a href="/wiki/Upington,_Northern_Cape" class="mw-redirect" title="Upington, Northern Cape">Upington</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> but this temperature is unofficial and was not recorded with standard equipment, the official highest temperature is 48.8&nbsp;°C (119.84&nbsp;°F) at <a href="/wiki/Vioolsdrif" title="Vioolsdrif">Vioolsdrif</a> in January 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt"> <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_South_Africa" title="Climate change in South Africa">Climate change in South Africa</a> is leading to increased temperatures and rainfall variability. Evidence shows that <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events are becoming more prominent due to climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_South_Africa_:4_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_South_Africa_:4-102">[102]</a></sup> This is a critical concern for South Africans as <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> will affect the overall status and wellbeing of the country, for example with regards to <a href="/wiki/Water_resources" title="Water resources">water resources</a>. Just like many other parts of the world, climate research showed that the real challenge in South Africa was more related to <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental issues in South Africa">environmental issues</a> raher than developmental ones.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The most severe effect will be targeting the <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a>, which has huge effects on the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> sector.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_South_Africa_:0_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_South_Africa_:0-104">[104]</a></sup> Speedy environmental changes are resulting in clear effects on the community and environmental level in different ways and aspects, starting with air quality, to temperature and <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather patterns</a>, reaching out to food security and disease burden.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_South_Africa" title="Biodiversity of South Africa">Biodiversity of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_South_Africa" title="Wildlife of South Africa">Wildlife of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas of South Africa">Protected areas of South Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marine_biodiversity_of_South_Africa" title="Marine biodiversity of South Africa">Marine biodiversity of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa signed the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on 4 June 1994, and became a party to the convention on 2 November 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_action_plan" title="Biodiversity action plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>, which was received by the convention on 7 June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-cbd.int_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbd.int-107">[107]</a></sup> The country is ranked sixth out of the world's seventeen <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism_in_South_Africa" title="Ecotourism in South Africa">Ecotourism in South Africa</a> has become more prevalent in recent years, as a possible method of maintaining and improving biodiversity. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:South_African_Giraffes,_fighting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg/220px-South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg/330px-South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg/440px-South_African_Giraffes%2C_fighting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1370" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:South_African_Giraffes,_fighting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/South_African_giraffe" title="South African giraffe">South African giraffes</a>, Kruger National Park
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Numerous mammals are found in the <a href="/wiki/Bushveld" title="Bushveld">Bushveld</a> including lions, <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">African leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_African_cheetah" class="mw-redirect" title="South African cheetah">South African cheetahs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_white_rhino" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern white rhino">southern white rhinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_wildebeest" title="Blue wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kudu" title="Kudu">kudus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Impala" title="Impala">impalas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">hyenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">hippopotamuses</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_African_giraffe" title="South African giraffe">South African giraffes</a>. A significant extent of the Bushveld exists in the north-east including <a href="/wiki/Kruger_National_Park" title="Kruger National Park">Kruger National Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sabi_Sand_Game_Reserve" title="Sabi Sand Game Reserve">Sabi Sand Game Reserve</a>, as well as in the far north in the <a href="/wiki/Waterberg_Biosphere" title="Waterberg Biosphere">Waterberg Biosphere</a>. South Africa houses many <a href="/wiki/Endemic_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic species">endemic species</a>, among them the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Riverine_rabbit" title="Riverine rabbit">riverine rabbit</a> (<i>Bunolagus monticullaris</i>) in the Karoo. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fungi">Fungi</span></h4> 
      <p>Up to 1945, more than 4900 species of <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Lichen#Fungi" title="Lichen">lichen-forming</a> species) had been recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2006, the number of fungi in South Africa was estimated at about 200,000 species, but did not take into account fungi associated with insects.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> If correct, then the number of South African fungi dwarfs that of its plants. In at least some major South African ecosystems, an exceptionally high percentage of fungi are highly specific in terms of the plants with which they occur.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The country's Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan does not mention fungi (including lichen-forming fungi).<sup id="cite_ref-cbd.int_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbd.int-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants">Plants</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg/220px-Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg/330px-Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg/440px-Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Forest_outside_of_Durban.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Subtropical forest near <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KNP_Landscape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KNP_Landscape.jpg/220px-KNP_Landscape.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KNP_Landscape.jpg/330px-KNP_Landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KNP_Landscape.jpg/440px-KNP_Landscape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KNP_Landscape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lowveld" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowveld">Lowveld</a> vegetation of the <a href="/wiki/Kruger_National_Park" title="Kruger National Park">Kruger National Park</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With more than 22,000 different <a href="/wiki/Higher_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Higher plants">higher plants</a>, or about 9% of all the known species of plants on Earth,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> South Africa is particularly rich in plant diversity. The most prevalent biome in South Africa is the <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grassland</a>, particularly on the Highveld, where the plant cover is dominated by different <a href="/wiki/Poaceae" title="Poaceae">grasses</a>, low <a href="/wiki/Shrub" title="Shrub">shrubs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Acacia_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Acacia tree">acacia trees</a>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Camelthorn_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Camelthorn tree">camel-thorn</a> (<i>Vachellia erioloba</i>). Vegetation becomes even more sparse towards the northwest due to low <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">rainfall</a>. There are several species of water-storing <a href="/wiki/Succulent_plant" title="Succulent plant">succulents</a>, like <a href="/wiki/Aloe" title="Aloe">aloes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euphorbias" class="mw-redirect" title="Euphorbias">euphorbias</a>, in the very hot and dry Namaqualand area. The grass and thorn <a href="/wiki/Savannah" class="mw-redirect" title="Savannah">savannah</a> turns slowly into a bush savannah towards the north-east of the country, with denser growth. There are significant numbers of <a href="/wiki/Baobab" class="mw-redirect" title="Baobab">baobab</a> trees in this area, near the northern end of Kruger National Park.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Fynbos" title="Fynbos">fynbos</a> biome, which makes up the majority of the area and plant life in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_floristic_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape floristic region">Cape floristic region</a>, one of the six <a href="/wiki/Floral_kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Floral kingdom">floral kingdoms</a>, is located in a small region of the Western Cape and contains more than 9,000 of those species, making it among the richest regions on earth in terms of plant diversity. Most of the plants are <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">evergreen</a> hard-leaf plants with fine, needle-like leaves, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sclerophyllous" class="mw-redirect" title="Sclerophyllous">sclerophyllous</a> plants. Another uniquely South African flowering plant group is the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Protea" title="Protea">Protea</a></i>. There are around 130 different species of Protea in South Africa. </p>
      <p>While South Africa has a great wealth of flowering plants, only one percent of South Africa is forest, almost exclusively in the humid <a href="/wiki/KwaZulu-Cape_coastal_forest_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="KwaZulu-Cape coastal forest mosaic">coastal plain of KwaZulu-Natal</a>, where there are also areas of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_mangroves" title="Southern Africa mangroves">Southern Africa mangroves</a> in river mouths. Even smaller reserves of forests are out of the reach of fire, known as <a href="/wiki/Knysna-Amatole_montane_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Knysna-Amatole montane forests">montane forests</a>. Plantations of imported tree species are predominant, particularly the non-native <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_issues">Conservation issues</span></h3> 
      <p>South Africa has lost a large area of natural habitat in the last four decades, primarily due to overpopulation, sprawling development patterns and deforestation during the 19th century. The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.94/10, ranking it 112th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-114">[114]</a></sup> South Africa is one of the worst affected countries in the world when it comes to invasion by <a href="/wiki/Alien_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Alien species">alien species</a> with many (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Acacia_mearnsii" title="Acacia mearnsii">black wattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acacia_saligna" title="Acacia saligna">Port Jackson willow</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hakea" title="Hakea">Hakea</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lantana" title="Lantana">Lantana</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jacaranda" title="Jacaranda">Jacaranda</a></i>) posing a significant threat to the native biodiversity and the already scarce water resources. The original <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests">temperate forest</a> found by the first European settlers was exploited ruthlessly until only small patches remained. Currently, South African <a href="/wiki/Hardwood" title="Hardwood">hardwood</a> trees like <a href="/wiki/Real_yellowwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Real yellowwood">real yellowwood</a> (<i>Podocarpus latifolius</i>), <a href="/wiki/Ocotea_bullata" title="Ocotea bullata">stinkwood</a> (<i>Ocotea bullata</i>), and South African <a href="/wiki/Olea_laurifolia" class="mw-redirect" title="Olea laurifolia">black ironwood</a> (<i>Olea laurifolia</i>) are under government protection. Statistics from the South African <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Environmental_Affairs" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Environmental Affairs">Department of Environmental Affairs</a> show a record 1,215 rhinos were killed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg/220px-Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg/330px-Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg/440px-Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas-114212.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cape_Floral_Region_Protected_Areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Floral Region Protected Areas">Cape Floral Region Protected Areas</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">Climate change</a> is expected to bring considerable warming and drying to much of this already <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-arid region">semi-arid region</a>, with greater frequency and intensity of extreme weather events such as <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat waves</a>, flooding and drought. According to computer-generated <a href="/wiki/Climate_modelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate modelling">climate modelling</a> produced by the South African National Biodiversity Institute,<sup id="cite_ref-SANBI_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANBI-116">[116]</a></sup> parts of southern Africa will see an increase in temperature by about 1&nbsp;°C (1.8&nbsp;°F) along the coast to more than 4&nbsp;°C (7.2&nbsp;°F) in the already hot <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> such as the Northern Cape in late spring and summertime by 2050. The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Floral_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Floral Region">Cape Floral Region</a>, being identified as one of the global <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspots" class="mw-redirect" title="Biodiversity hotspots">biodiversity hotspots</a>, will be hit very hard by climate change. Drought, increased intensity and frequency of fire, and climbing temperatures are expected to push many rare species towards extinction. South Africa has published two national climate change reports in 2011 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_South_Africa" title="Government of South Africa">Government of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_South_Africa" title="Politics of South Africa">Politics of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_of_South_Africa" title="Law of South Africa">Law of South Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_South_Africa" title="Human rights in South Africa">Human rights in South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Uniegebou.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photo of the Union Buildings" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/220px-Uniegebou.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/330px-Uniegebou.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Uniegebou.jpg/440px-Uniegebou.jpg 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="514"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Uniegebou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Union_Buildings" title="Union Buildings">Union Buildings</a> in Pretoria, seat of the executive
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Houses_of_Parliament_(Cape_Town).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg/220px-Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg/330px-Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg/440px-Houses_of_Parliament_%28Cape_Town%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2274" data-file-height="1893"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Houses_of_Parliament_(Cape_Town).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Houses of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa" title="Parliament of South Africa">Parliament</a> in Cape Town, seat of the legislature
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, although unlike most such republics the <a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Africa" title="President of South Africa">President</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and depends for his tenure on the <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">confidence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa" title="Parliament of South Africa">Parliament</a>. The executive, legislature and judiciary are all subject to the supremacy of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_South_Africa" title="Courts of South Africa">superior courts</a> have the power to strike down executive actions and acts of Parliament if they are unconstitutional. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_South_Africa" title="National Assembly of South Africa">National Assembly</a>, the lower house of Parliament, consists of 400 members and is elected every five years by a system of <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Provinces" title="National Council of Provinces">National Council of Provinces</a>, the upper house, consists of ninety members, with each of the nine <a href="/wiki/Provincial_legislature_(South_Africa)" title="Provincial legislature (South Africa)">provincial legislatures</a> electing ten members. </p>
      <p>After each parliamentary election, the National Assembly elects one of its members as president; hence the President serves a term of office the same as that of the Assembly, normally five years. No President may serve more than two terms in office.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The President appoints a <a href="/wiki/Deputy_President_of_South_Africa" title="Deputy President of South Africa">Deputy President</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">Ministers</a>, who form the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_South_Africa" title="Cabinet of South Africa">Cabinet</a> which consists of <a href="/wiki/Departmentalization" title="Departmentalization">Departments</a>. The National Assembly may remove the President and the Cabinet by a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">motion of no confidence</a>. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2019_South_African_general_election" title="2019 South African general election">most recent election</a>, held on 8 May 2019, the ANC won 57.5% of the vote and 230 seats, while the main opposition, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(South_Africa)" title="Democratic Alliance (South Africa)">Democratic Alliance</a> (DA) won 20.77% of the vote and 84 seats. The <a href="/wiki/Economic_Freedom_Fighters" title="Economic Freedom Fighters">Economic Freedom Fighters</a> (EFF), founded by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Malema" title="Julius Malema">Julius Malema</a>, former President of the ANC's Youth Wing (<a href="/wiki/ANC_Youth_League" class="mw-redirect" title="ANC Youth League">ANC Youth League</a>) who was later expelled from the ANC, won 10.79% of the vote and 44 seats. The ANC has been the governing political party in South Africa since the end of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>. </p>
      <p>South Africa has no legally defined capital city. The fourth chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution of South Africa</a>, states that "The seat of Parliament is Cape Town, but an Act of Parliament enacted in accordance with section 76(1) and (5) may determine that the seat of Parliament is elsewhere."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The country's three branches of government are split over different cities. <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, as the seat of Parliament, is the legislative capital; <a href="/wiki/Pretoria" title="Pretoria">Pretoria</a>, as the seat of the President and Cabinet, is the administrative capital; and <a href="/wiki/Bloemfontein" title="Bloemfontein">Bloemfontein</a>, as the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Appeal_of_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Court of Appeal of South Africa">Supreme Court of Appeal</a>, is the judicial capital, while the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Constitutional Court of South Africa">Constitutional Court of South Africa</a> sits in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>. Most foreign embassies are located in Pretoria. </p>
      <p>Since 2004, South Africa has had many thousands of popular protests, some violent, making it, according to one academic, the "most protest-rich country in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> There have been a number of incidents of <a href="/wiki/Political_repression_in_post-Apartheid_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Political repression in post-Apartheid South Africa">political repression</a> as well as threats of future repression in violation of the constitution, leading some analysts and <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> organisations to conclude that there is or could be a new climate of political repression,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> or a decline in political tolerance.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, South Africa placed fifth out of 48 <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan African</a> countries on the <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>. South Africa scored well in the categories of <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Rule of Law">Rule of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transparency_(social)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transparency (social)">Transparency</a> and Corruption, and <a href="/wiki/Participation_(decision_making)" class="mw-redirect" title="Participation (decision making)">Participation</a> and Human Rights, but was let down by its relatively poor performance in Safety and Security.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In November 2006, South Africa became the first African country to legalise <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_South_Africa" title="Crime in South Africa">Crime in South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photo of the Constitutional Court" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg/220px-ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg/330px-ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg/440px-ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ConstitutionalCourtofSouthAfrica-entrance-20070622.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Constitutional Court of South Africa">Constitutional Court</a> in Johannesburg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution of South Africa</a> is the supreme <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> in the country. The primary sources of <a href="/wiki/South_African_law" class="mw-redirect" title="South African law">South African law</a> are <a href="/wiki/Roman-Dutch_law" title="Roman-Dutch law">Roman-Dutch mercantile law</a> and personal law with <a href="/wiki/English_Common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English Common law">English Common law</a>, as imports of Dutch settlements and <a href="/wiki/British_colonialism" class="mw-redirect" title="British colonialism">British colonialism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The first European based law in South Africa was brought by the Dutch East India Company and is called Roman-Dutch law. It was imported before the <a href="/wiki/Codification_(law)" title="Codification (law)">codification</a> of European law into the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a> and is comparable in many ways to <a href="/wiki/Scots_law" title="Scots law">Scots law</a>. This was followed in the 19th century by <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English law</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common</a> and <a href="/wiki/Statutory_law" title="Statutory law">statutory</a>. After unification in 1910, South Africa had its own parliament which passed laws specific for South Africa, building on those previously passed for the individual member colonies. </p>
      <p>The judicial system consists of the <a href="/wiki/Magistrates%27_Courts_of_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Magistrates' Courts of South Africa">magistrates' courts</a>, which hear lesser criminal cases and smaller civil cases; the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_South_Africa" title="High Court of South Africa">High Court</a>, which has divisions that serve as the courts of <a href="/wiki/General_jurisdiction" title="General jurisdiction">general jurisdiction</a> for specific areas; the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Appeal_of_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Court of Appeal of South Africa">Supreme Court of Appeal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Constitutional Court of South Africa">Constitutional Court</a>, which is the highest court. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dying_For_Justice_(8036294736).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg/220px-Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg/330px-Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg/440px-Dying_For_Justice_%288036294736%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="617"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dying_For_Justice_(8036294736).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Soweto Pride 2012 participants protest against violence against lesbians. The country has strong human rights laws but some groups are still discriminated against. It is the first country in Africa to recognise <a href="/wiki/Same_sex_marriage" class="mw-redirect" title="Same sex marriage">same sex marriage</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From April 2017 to March 2018, on average 57 murders were committed each day in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In the year ended March 2017, there were 20,336 murders and the murder rate was 35.9 per 100,000 – over five times higher than the global average of 6.2 per 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Middle-class South Africans seek security in <a href="/wiki/Gated_community" title="Gated community">gated communities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Private_security_industry_in_South_Africa" title="Private security industry in South Africa">private security industry in South Africa</a> is the largest in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> with nearly 9,000 registered companies and 400,000 registered active private security guards, more than the South African police and army combined.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Many emigrants from South Africa also state that crime was a major factor in their decision to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_African_Farmer_Murders" class="mw-redirect" title="South African Farmer Murders">Crime against the farming community</a> has continued to be a major problem.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In an attempt to reduce crime rate, the police arrested over 500 undocumented foreigners in a raid in August 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>South Africa has a high rape rate, with 43,195 rapes reported in 2014/15, and an unknown number of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexual assaults</a> going unreported.<sup id="cite_ref-africaCheckRapeStats_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africaCheckRapeStats-135">[135]</a></sup> A 2009 survey of 1,738 men in KwaZulu-Natal and the Eastern Cape by the Medical Research Council found one in four men admitted to raping someone<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and another survey of 4,000 women in Johannesburg by CIET Africa found one in three said they had been raped in the past year.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-137">[137]</a></sup> Rape occurs most commonly in relationships, but many men and women say that rape cannot occur in relationships; however, one in four women reported having been abused by an intimate partner.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrahams_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrahams-138">[138]</a></sup> Rapes are also perpetrated by children (some as young as ten).<sup id="cite_ref-medscape_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medscape-139">[139]</a></sup> The incidence of <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child and infant rape</a> is among the highest in the world, largely as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_cleansing_myth" title="Virgin cleansing myth">virgin cleansing myth</a>, and a number of high-profile cases (sometimes as young as eight months)<sup id="cite_ref-medscape_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medscape-139">[139]</a></sup> have outraged the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-time_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-140">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 1994 and 2018, there were more than 500 xenophobic <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia_in_South_Africa" title="Xenophobia in South Africa">attacks against foreigners</a> in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2019_Johannesburg_riots" title="2019 Johannesburg riots">2019 Johannesburg riots</a> were similar in nature and origin to the <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia_in_South_Africa#May_2008_riots" title="Xenophobia in South Africa">2008 xenophobic riots</a> that also occurred in Johannesburg.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_South_Africa" title="Foreign relations of South Africa">Foreign relations of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BRICS_leaders_family_photo,_2018_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg/220px-BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg/330px-BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg/440px-BRICS_leaders_family_photo%2C_2018_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1140" data-file-height="760"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BRICS_leaders_family_photo,_2018_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Leaders of the <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a> nations at the <a href="/wiki/10th_BRICS_summit" title="10th BRICS summit">10th BRICS summit</a> in Johannesburg, South Africa, 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As the Union of South Africa, the country was a founding member of the UN. The then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smuts" title="Jan Smuts">Jan Smuts</a> wrote the <a href="/wiki/Preamble_to_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Preamble to the United Nations Charter">preamble to the UN Charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gildersleeve_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gildersleeve-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schlesinger_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schlesinger-144">[144]</a></sup> South Africa is one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU), and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of African countries by GDP (nominal)">third largest economy of all the members</a>. It is also a founding member of the AU's <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa's Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD). </p>
      <p>South Africa has played a key role as a mediator in African conflicts over the last decade, such as in <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> (DRC), the <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a>, and Zimbabwe. After apartheid ended, South Africa was readmitted to the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">Group of 77</a> and chaired the organisation in 2006. South Africa is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC), <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone" title="South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone">South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (SACU), <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">Antarctic Treaty System</a> (ATS), <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a href="/wiki/G20_industrial_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="G20 industrial nations">G20</a>, <a href="/wiki/G8%2B5" title="G8+5">G8+5</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Port_Management_Association_of_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa">Port Management Association of Eastern and Southern Africa</a>. </p>
      <p>Former South African President <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a> and former Chinese President <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> upgraded bilateral ties between the two countries on 24 August 2010, when they signed the Beijing Agreement, which elevated South Africa's earlier "strategic partnership" with China to the higher level of "comprehensive strategic partnership" in both economic and political affairs, including the strengthening of exchanges between their respective ruling parties and legislatures.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> In April 2011, South Africa formally joined the Brazil-Russia-India-China (<a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a>) grouping of countries, identified by Zuma as the country's largest trading partners, and also the largest trading partners with Africa as a whole. Zuma asserted that BRICS member countries would also work with each other through the UN, the Group of Twenty (G20) and the India, Brazil South Africa (<a href="/wiki/IBSA_Dialogue_Forum" title="IBSA Dialogue Forum">IBSA</a>) forum.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_(8724689015).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg/220px-Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg/330px-Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg/440px-Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_%288724689015%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roodewal_Weapons_Range_-_(8724689015).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">SANDF</a> soldiers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a> (SANDF) was created in 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-1993-224_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-1993-224-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> as an <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_military" title="Volunteer military">all-volunteer military</a> composed of the former <a href="/wiki/South_African_Defence_Force" title="South African Defence Force">South African Defence Force</a>, the forces of the African nationalist groups (<span lang="xh" style="font-style: normal;" title="Xhosa-language text"><a href="/wiki/UMkhonto_we_Sizwe" title="UMkhonto we Sizwe">uMkhonto we Sizwe</a></span> and <a href="/wiki/Azanian_People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="Azanian People's Liberation Army">Azanian People's Liberation Army</a>), and the former Bantustan defence forces.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-1993-224_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-1993-224-148">[148]</a></sup> The SANDF is subdivided into four branches, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Army" title="South African Army">South African Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Air_Force" title="South African Air Force">South African Air Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Navy" title="South African Navy">South African Navy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Military_Health_Service" title="South African Military Health Service">South African Military Health Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-act-42-2002_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-act-42-2002-150">[150]</a></sup> In recent years, the SANDF has become a major <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> force in Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dod-sep2005-151">[151]</a></sup> and has been involved in operations in Lesotho, the DRC,<sup id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dod-sep2005-151">[151]</a></sup> and Burundi,<sup id="cite_ref-dod-sep2005_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dod-sep2005-151">[151]</a></sup> amongst others. It has also served in multinational <a href="/wiki/UN_Peacekeeping_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Peacekeeping forces">UN Peacekeeping forces</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">UN Force Intervention Brigade</a> for example. </p>
      <p>South Africa is the only African country to have successfully developed <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons and South Africa">nuclear weapons</a>. It became the first country (followed by <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>) with nuclear capability to voluntarily renounce and dismantle its programme and in the process signed the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty">Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-fas-ocp27_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fas-ocp27-152">[152]</a></sup> South Africa undertook a <a href="/wiki/South_African_nuclear_program" class="mw-redirect" title="South African nuclear program">nuclear weapons programme</a> in the 1970s<sup id="cite_ref-fas-ocp27_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fas-ocp27-152">[152]</a></sup> According to former state president <a href="/wiki/FW_de_Klerk" class="mw-redirect" title="FW de Klerk">FW de Klerk</a>, the decision to build a "nuclear deterrent" was taken "as early as 1974 against a backdrop of a Soviet expansionist threat."<sup id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-153">[153]</a></sup> South Africa is <a href="/wiki/Vela_Incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Vela Incident">alleged to have conducted</a> a nuclear test over the Atlantic in 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> although this is officially denied. Former president de Klerk maintained that South Africa had "never conducted a clandestine nuclear test."<sup id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-153">[153]</a></sup> Six nuclear devices were completed between 1980 and 1990, but all were dismantled before South Africa signed the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-South_Africa_comes_clean_153-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Africa_comes_clean-153">[153]</a></sup> In 2017, South Africa signed the UN treaty on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_South_Africa" title="Provinces of South Africa">Provinces of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/330px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/495px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg/660px-Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="809" data-file-height="709"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_South_Africa_with_English_labels.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_South_Africa" title="Provinces of South Africa">Provinces of South Africa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Each of the nine provinces is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Provincial_legislature_(South_Africa)" title="Provincial legislature (South Africa)">legislature</a>, which is elected every five years by <a href="/wiki/Party-list_proportional_representation" title="Party-list proportional representation">party-list proportional representation</a>. The legislature elects a <a href="/wiki/Premier_(South_Africa)" title="Premier (South Africa)">Premier</a> as head of government, and the Premier appoints an <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_(South_Africa)" title="Executive Council (South Africa)">Executive Council</a> as a provincial cabinet. The powers of provincial governments are limited to topics listed in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution</a>; these topics include such fields as health, education, public housing and transport. </p>
      <p>The provinces are in turn divided into 52 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_South_Africa" title="Districts of South Africa">districts</a>: 8 <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_municipality_(South_Africa)" title="Metropolitan municipality (South Africa)">metropolitan</a> and 44 <a href="/wiki/District_municipality_(South_Africa)" class="mw-redirect" title="District municipality (South Africa)">district municipalities</a>. The district municipalities are further subdivided into 205 <a href="/wiki/Local_municipality_(South_Africa)" title="Local municipality (South Africa)">local municipalities</a>. The metropolitan municipalities, which govern the largest urban agglomerations, perform the functions of both district and local municipalities. </p>
