      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_South_Africa" title="Economy of South Africa">Economy of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=File:Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg&amp;lang=en" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg/330px-Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg/495px-Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg/660px-Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1354" data-file-height="812"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Annual_per_capita_personal_income_by_race_group_in_South_Africa_relative_to_white_levels.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Annual <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Per capita personal income">per capita personal income</a> by race group in South Africa relative to white levels
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/170px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/255px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg/340px-Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1429" data-file-height="2168"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/JSE_Limited" title="JSE Limited">Johannesburg Stock Exchange</a> (JSE) is the largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> on the African continent
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>, the second largest in Africa after <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. It also has a relatively high gross domestic product (GDP) per capita compared to other countries in sub-Saharan Africa (US$11,750 at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> as of 2012). Despite this, South Africa is still burdened by a relatively high rate of poverty and unemployment, and is also ranked in the top ten countries in the world for <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality" class="mw-redirect" title="Income inequality">income inequality</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> measured by the <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a>. In 2015, 71 percent of net wealth are held by 10 percent richest of the population, whereas 60 percent of the poorest held only 7 percent of the net wealth and the Gini coefficient was 0.63, whereas in 1996 was 0.61.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unlike most of the world's poor countries, South Africa does not have a thriving <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal economy</a>. Only 15% of South African jobs are in the <a href="/wiki/Informal_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Informal sector">informal sector</a>, compared with around half in <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Brazil" title="Economy of Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">India</a> and nearly three-quarters in <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Indonesia" title="Economy of Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD) attributes this difference to South Africa's widespread welfare system.<sup id="cite_ref-economist1_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist1-162">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> research shows that South Africa has one of the widest gaps between per capita GDP versus its <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) ranking, with only <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> showing a larger gap.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After 1994, government policy brought down inflation, stabilised public finances, and some foreign capital was attracted, however growth was still subpar.<sup id="cite_ref-assessment2008-2_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assessment2008-2-164">[164]</a></sup> From 2004 onward, economic growth picked up significantly; both employment and <a href="/wiki/Capital_formation" title="Capital formation">capital formation</a> increased.<sup id="cite_ref-assessment2008-2_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assessment2008-2-164">[164]</a></sup> During the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a>, the government increased the role of <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">state-owned enterprises</a> (SOEs). Some of the biggest SOEs are <a href="/wiki/Eskom" title="Eskom">Eskom</a>, the electric power monopoly, <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">South African Airways</a> (SAA), and <a href="/wiki/Transnet" title="Transnet">Transnet</a>, the railroad and ports monopoly. Some of these SOEs have not been profitable, such as SAA, which has required bailouts totaling R30&nbsp;billion ($2.08 billion) over the 20 years preceding 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Principal international trading partners of South Africa—besides other African countries—include Germany, the United States, China, Japan, the United Kingdom and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-166">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_South_Africa" title="Agriculture in South Africa">South African agricultural industry</a> contributes around 10% of formal employment, relatively low compared to other parts of Africa, as well as providing work for casual labourers and contributing around 2.6% of GDP for the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-167">[167]</a></sup> Due to the <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">aridity</a> of the land, only 13.5% can be used for crop production, and only 3% is considered high potential land.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2013, South Africa was ranked as the top African Country of the Future by <i><a href="/wiki/FDi_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="FDi magazine">fDi magazine</a></i> based on the country's <a href="/wiki/Economic_potential" title="Economic potential">economic potential</a>, labour environment, cost-effectiveness, infrastructure, business friendliness, and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2020 <a href="/wiki/Financial_Secrecy_Index" title="Financial Secrecy Index">Financial Secrecy Index</a> (FDI) ranks South Africa as the 58th safest tax haven in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_South_Africa" title="Tourism in South Africa">Tourism in South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa is a popular tourist destination, and a substantial amount of revenue comes from tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg/220px-Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg/330px-Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg/440px-Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="828" data-file-height="637"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Graaff_Fruit-Ceres_packing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Workers packing pears for export in the <a href="/wiki/Ceres,_Western_Cape" title="Ceres, Western Cape">Ceres Valley</a>, Western Cape
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During 1995–2003, the number of formal jobs decreased and informal jobs increased; overall unemployment worsened.<sup id="cite_ref-sach3_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sach3-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government's <a href="/wiki/Black_Economic_Empowerment" title="Black Economic Empowerment">Black Economic Empowerment</a> (BEE) policies have drawn criticism from Neva Makgetla, lead economist for research and information at the <a href="/wiki/Development_Bank_of_Southern_Africa" title="Development Bank of Southern Africa">Development Bank of Southern Africa</a>, for focusing "almost exclusively on promoting individual ownership by black people [which] does little to address broader economic disparities, though the rich may become more diverse."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Official <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> policies have seen a rise in black economic wealth and an emerging black middle class.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Other problems include <a href="/wiki/State_ownership" title="State ownership">state ownership</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_intervention" class="mw-redirect" title="State intervention">interference</a>, which impose high barriers to entry in many areas.<sup id="cite_ref-assessment2008_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assessment2008-174">[174]</a></sup> Restrictive <a href="/wiki/Labour_regulations" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour regulations">labour regulations</a> have contributed to the unemployment malaise.<sup id="cite_ref-sach3_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sach3-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Along with many African nations, South Africa has been experiencing a <a href="/wiki/Brain_drain" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain drain">brain drain</a> in the past 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> and is almost certainly detrimental for the wellbeing of those reliant on the healthcare infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> The skills drain in South Africa tends to demonstrate racial contours given the skills distribution legacy of South Africa and has thus resulted in large white South African communities abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> However, the statistics which purport to show a brain drain are disputed and also do not account for <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">repatriation</a> and expiry of foreign work contracts. According to several surveys,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> there has been a reverse in brain drain following the <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_crisis_of_2008%E2%80%932009" class="mw-redirect" title="Global financial crisis of 2008–2009">global financial crisis of 2008–2009</a> and expiration of foreign work contracts. In the first quarter of 2011, confidence levels for graduate professionals were recorded at a level of 84% in a Professional Provident Society (PPS) survey.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Illegal immigrants are involved in informal trading.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Many immigrants to South Africa continue to live in poor conditions, and the immigration policy has become increasingly restrictive since the year 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Human Rights Watch reported on 26 August 2019 about foreign national truck drivers being subjected to deadly attacks carried out by South African truck drivers. The organization urged the South African government to take immediate actions ensuring the safety of the foreign national truck drivers putting up with violence, harassment, intimidation, stoning, bombing, and shooting, by local truck drivers in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_South_Africa" title="Science and technology in South Africa">Science and technology in South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/220px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/330px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg/440px-Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1356" data-file-height="1100"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Shuttleworth_NASA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth" title="Mark Shuttleworth">Mark Shuttleworth</a> in space
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Several important scientific and technological developments have originated in South Africa. The first human-to-human <a href="/wiki/Heart_transplantation" title="Heart transplantation">heart transplant</a> was performed by cardiac surgeon <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Barnard" title="Christiaan Barnard">Christiaan Barnard</a> at <a href="/wiki/Groote_Schuur_Hospital" title="Groote Schuur Hospital">Groote Schuur Hospital</a> in December 1967, <a href="/wiki/Max_Theiler" title="Max Theiler">Max Theiler</a> developed a <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever_vaccine" title="Yellow fever vaccine">vaccine</a> against <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allan_McLeod_Cormack" class="mw-redirect" title="Allan McLeod Cormack">Allan McLeod Cormack</a> pioneered <a href="/wiki/X-ray_computed_tomography" class="mw-redirect" title="X-ray computed tomography">X-ray computed tomography</a> (CT scan), and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Klug" title="Aaron Klug">Aaron Klug</a> developed <a href="/wiki/Crystallographic_electron_microscopy" class="mw-redirect" title="Crystallographic electron microscopy">crystallographic electron microscopy</a> techniques. With the exception of that of Barnard, all of these advancements were recognised with Nobel Prizes. <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Brenner" title="Sydney Brenner">Sydney Brenner</a> won most recently, in 2002, for his pioneering work in <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mark_Shuttleworth" title="Mark Shuttleworth">Mark Shuttleworth</a> founded an early Internet security company <a href="/wiki/Thawte" title="Thawte">Thawte</a>, that was subsequently bought out by world-leader <a href="/wiki/VeriSign" class="mw-redirect" title="VeriSign">VeriSign</a>. Despite government efforts to encourage entrepreneurship in <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, information technology and other high technology fields, no other notable groundbreaking companies have been founded in South Africa.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It is the expressed objective of the government to transition the economy to be more reliant on high technology, based on the realisation that South Africa cannot compete with Far Eastern economies in manufacturing, nor can the republic rely on its mineral wealth in perpetuity. </p>
      <p>South Africa has cultivated a burgeoning <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a> community. It hosts the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Large_Telescope" title="Southern African Large Telescope">Southern African Large Telescope</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Optical_telescope" title="Optical telescope">optical telescope</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>. South Africa is currently building the <a href="/wiki/Karoo_Array_Telescope" class="mw-redirect" title="Karoo Array Telescope">Karoo Array Telescope</a> as a pathfinder for the €1.5&nbsp;billion <a href="/wiki/Square_Kilometre_Array" title="Square Kilometre Array">Square Kilometre Array</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> On 25 May 2012, it was announced that hosting of the Square Kilometer Array Telescope will be split over both the South African and the Australia and New Zealand sites.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-185">[185]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_South_Africa" title="Water supply and sanitation in South Africa">Water supply and sanitation in South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Two distinctive features of the South African water sector are the policy of free basic water and the existence of <a href="/wiki/Water_Board_(South_Africa)" title="Water Board (South Africa)">water boards</a>, which are bulk water supply agencies that operate pipelines and sell water from reservoirs to municipalities. These features have led to significant problems concerning the financial sustainability of service providers, leading to a lack of attention to maintenance. Following the end of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, the country had made improvements in the levels of access to water as those with access increased from 66% to 79% from 1990 to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-186">[186]</a></sup> Sanitation access increased from 71% to 79% during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-186">[186]</a></sup> However, water supply and sanitation in South Africa has come under increasing pressure in recent years despite a commitment made by the government to improve service standards and provide investment subsidies to the water industry.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The eastern parts of South Africa suffer from periodic droughts linked to the <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a> weather phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation-188">[188]</a></sup> In early 2018, Cape Town, which has different weather patterns to the rest of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whyCapeTownDroughtConversation-188">[188]</a></sup> faced a water crisis as the city's water supply was predicted to run dry before the end of June. Water-saving measures were in effect that required each citizen to use less than 50 litres (13&nbsp;US&nbsp;gal) a day.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_South_Africa" title="Transport in South Africa">Transport in South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Different methods of transport in South Africa include roads, railways, airports, water, and pipelines for petroleum oil. The majority of people in South Africa use informal <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">minibus taxis</a> as their main mode of transport. <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">BRT</a> has been implemented in some South African cities in an attempt to provide more formalised and safer public transport services. These systems have been widely criticised due to their large capital and operating costs. A "freeway" is different from most countries as certain things are forbidden which include certain motorcycles, no hand signals, and motor tricycles. South Africa has many major ports including Cape Town, <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth" title="Port Elizabeth">Port Elizabeth</a> that allow ships and other boats to pass through, some carrying passengers and some carrying <a href="/wiki/Oil_tanker" title="Oil tanker">petroleum tankers</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_South_Africa" title="Demographics of South Africa">Demographics of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_(hex_cells).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg/220px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg/330px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg/440px-South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_%28hex_cells%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="807" data-file-height="711"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_2011_population_density_map_(hex_cells).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of population density in South Africa
         <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1022511316">.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key{column-count:2}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key-wide{column-count:3}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key-narrow{column-count:1}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key>ol{margin-left:1.3em;margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key>ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .thumb .image-key li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
         <div class="plainlist image-key">
          <ul>

         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa is a nation of about 55 million (2016) people of diverse origins, cultures, languages, and religions. The last <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_2011" title="South African National Census of 2011">census</a> was held in 2011, with a more recent intercensal national survey conducted in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> South Africa is home to an estimated five&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal immigrant">illegal immigrants</a>, including some three&nbsp;million Zimbabweans.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> A series of <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Africa_riots" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Africa riots">anti-immigrant riots</a> occurred in South Africa beginning on 11 May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Statistics_South_Africa" title="Statistics South Africa">Statistics South Africa</a> asks people to describe themselves in the census in terms of five <a href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (classification of human beings)">racial</a> population groups.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The 2011 census figures for these groups were: <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples_in_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu peoples in South Africa">Black African</a> at 79.2%, <a href="/wiki/White_South_African" class="mw-redirect" title="White South African">White</a> at 8.9%, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Coloureds" title="Cape Coloureds">Coloured</a> at 8.9%, <a href="/wiki/Indian_South_Africans" title="Indian South Africans">Indian or Asian</a> at 2.5%, and Other/Unspecified at 0.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-cib11_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>21</span></sup> The first census in South Africa in 1911 showed that whites made up 22% of the population; this had declined to 16% by 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>South Africa hosts a sizeable refugee and asylum seeker population. According to the <i>World Refugee Survey 2008</i>, published by the <a href="/wiki/US_Committee_for_Refugees_and_Immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants">US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants</a>, this population numbered approximately 144,700 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-198">[198]</a></sup> Groups of refugees and asylum seekers numbering over 10,000 included people from Zimbabwe (48,400), the DRC (24,800), and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> (12,900).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-198">[198]</a></sup> These populations mainly lived in Johannesburg, Pretoria, <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a>, Cape Town, and <a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth" title="Port Elizabeth">Port Elizabeth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_198-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-198">[198]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Africa" title="Languages of South Africa">Languages of South Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">

          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#d0d0d0; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;None dominant
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ffffff; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Areas of little or no population
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Africa has 11 official languages:<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_African_English" title="South African English">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Sotho">Pedi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Tswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sotho_language" title="Sotho language">Southern Sotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">Tsonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swazi_language" title="Swazi language">Swazi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venda_language" title="Venda language">Venda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ndebele_language" title="Southern Ndebele language">Southern Ndebele</a> (in order of first language speakers). In this regard it is fourth only to <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Official languages of India">India</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> in number. While all the languages are formally equal, some languages are spoken more than others. According to the 2011 census, the three most spoken first languages are Zulu (22.7%), Xhosa (16.0%), and Afrikaans (13.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-cib11_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-9">[9]</a></sup> Although English is recognised as the language of commerce and science, it is only the fourth most common home language, that of only 9.6% of South Africans in 2011; nevertheless, it has become the de facto <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-cib11_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cib11-9">[9]</a></sup> Estimates based on the 1991 census suggest just under half of South Africans can speak English.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> It is the second most commonly spoken language outside of the household, after Zulu.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country also recognises several unofficial languages, including <a href="/wiki/Fanagalo_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Fanagalo language">Fanagalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khoe_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Khoe language">Khoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobedu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lobedu language">Lobedu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nama_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nama language">Nama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_language" title="Northern Ndebele language">Northern Ndebele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phuthi_language" title="Phuthi language">Phuthi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_African_Sign_Language" title="South African Sign Language">South African Sign Language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> These unofficial languages may be used in certain official uses in limited areas where it has been determined that these languages are prevalent. </p>
      <p>Many of the unofficial <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">languages of the San and Khoekhoe</a> peoples contain regional dialects stretching northwards into Namibia and Botswana, and elsewhere. These people, who are a physically distinct population from the Bantu people who make up most of the Black Africans in South Africa, have their own cultural identity based on their <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> societies. They have been marginalised to a great extent, and the remainder of their languages are in danger of becoming <a href="/wiki/Extinct_language" title="Extinct language">extinct</a>. </p>
      <p>White South Africans may also speak <a href="/wiki/European_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="European languages">European languages</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> (also spoken by black Angolans and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambicans</a>), <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, while some Indian South Africans speak <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India" title="Languages of India">Indian languages</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urdu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Urdu language">Urdu</a>. <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is spoken in South Africa by migrants from <a href="/wiki/Francophone_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone Africa">Francophone Africa</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_centres">Urban centres</span></h3> 
      <p>One online database<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> lists South Africa having more than 12,600 cities and towns. The following are the largest cities and towns in South Africa. </p>
